  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_159e9b11-b824-4e96-beeb-295f9920058a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer323452340176237186">Seventeen-year-old Cassie is a natural at reading people. Piecing together the tiniest details, she can tell you who you are and what you want. But it’s not a skill that she’s ever taken seriously. That is, until the FBI come knocking: they’ve begun a classified program that uses exceptional teenagers to crack infamous cold cases, and they need Cassie.<br/><br/>What Cassie doesn’t r</span>
  <span id="freeText323452340176237186" style="display:none">Seventeen-year-old Cassie is a natural at reading people. Piecing together the tiniest details, she can tell you who you are and what you want. But it’s not a skill that she’s ever taken seriously. That is, until the FBI come knocking: they’ve begun a classified program that uses exceptional teenagers to crack infamous cold cases, and they need Cassie.<br /><br />What Cassie doesn’t realize is that there’s more at risk than a few unsolved homicides—especially when she’s sent to live with a group of teens whose gifts are as unusual as her own. Sarcastic, privileged Michael has a knack for reading emotions, which he uses to get inside Cassie’s head—and under her skin. Brooding Dean shares Cassie’s gift for profiling, but keeps her at arm’s length.<br /><br />Soon, it becomes clear that no one in the Naturals program is what they seem. And when a new killer strikes, danger looms closer than Cassie could ever have imagined. Caught in a lethal game of cat and mouse with a killer, the Naturals are going to have to use all of their gifts just to survive.</span>
  <a data-text-id="323452340176237186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/43990213-kyleigh"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1434404521i/43990213._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/43990213-kyleigh">Kyleigh</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I wasn't sure when I started reading if it was going to be, since the first case had such a personal connection to Cassie and I wasn't sure Barnes wou<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I wasn't sure when I started reading if it was going to be, since the first case had such a personal connection to Cassie and I wasn't sure Barnes would be able to follow that up with something that would wow me yet again. But I have to admit that she did. While the first book had the big reveal at the end, this one kind of revealed stuff along the way (sorry, I'm trying not to give stuff away). So naturally (haha) the second book didn't have the same effect, but the tension was REAL. Loved them both<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="bookReviews">
  




  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_651336002" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/651336002" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/651336002?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=tstl">tstl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=detective">detective</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=slut-shaming">slut-shaming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=shits-and-giggles">shits-and-giggles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=jericho-fucking-barrons">jericho-fucking-barrons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=middle-school">middle-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mary-sue">mary-sue</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer651336002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3821329435830338970"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383976085ra/6727951.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>This book is <i>Criminal Minds</i> fanfiction, for the under-15 crowd.</b> It takes a great deal of suspension of disbelief to read this book; and I'm not talking about the preposterousness of the idea that children---teenagers, can be FBI criminal investigators. <b>The necessary suspension of disbelief from the reader's part is required in order to swallow the fact that a bunch of utterly incompetent, petty teenagers are capable of looking beyond their egotistical, self-centered noses.</b><br/><br/>There's this show I lov</span>
  <span id="freeText3821329435830338970" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383976085ra/6727951.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This book is <i>Criminal Minds</i> fanfiction, for the under-15 crowd.</b> It takes a great deal of suspension of disbelief to read this book; and I'm not talking about the preposterousness of the idea that children---teenagers, can be FBI criminal investigators. <b>The necessary suspension of disbelief from the reader's part is required in order to swallow the fact that a bunch of utterly incompetent, petty teenagers are capable of looking beyond their egotistical, self-centered noses.</b><br><br>There's this show I love called <i>Criminal Minds</i>. It features a team of FBI profilers at the Behavioral Analysis Unit. They take on difficult cases, involving mainly serial killers. The special agents make psychological profiles about the potential suspect, then using that information, narrow down the field of suspect until they get the right one. The show is entertainment, there is no argument on my part about that. Behavioral analysis is a bullshit art, at best. Criminal profilers have rarely been right, it's more of a matter of throwing a rock into the darkness in the hopes of eventually hitting someone in the face. It rarely happens, but they get it right sometimes. More than anything, it is a show with likeable, complex characters, and a wonderful team who puts their personal problems and quirks aside to work together like a well-oiled machine in order to solve a case.<br><br>Well-oiled machine is not the word I would use to describe the characters in this book and their cohesiveness. <b>The teenagers in this book work together as well as an AK-47 that's been left to rust for 50 years in the mud of a long-forgotten battlefield; the parts do not function, and the damn gun might blow up and shoot you by accident in the face at any given moment.</b><br><br>Still, this book is based on that premise. It is a team of teen profilers who use the word "UNSUB" to describe an unknown subject. The word UNSUB is strictly a TV-based term, and it was Criminal Minds that popularized the use of the word. <b>To me, this is nothing more than adolescent Criminal Minds fanfiction, without the likeable, complex characters.</b><br><br><u>Summary</u>: 17-year old Cassandra (Cassie) lives with her large extended Italian family, working part-time as a waitress. Her mother has been murdered 5 years ago, and her father is out of the picture (<b>see what I mean about parents in YA fiction? Dead or gone 90% of the time</b>). Cassie has always had a skill for reading people, for predicting what they want. Right now, her skills are being used for nothing more than to predict what her customers are going to order next from the menu. A boy, a <i>sexy</i> boy appears from nowhere, well-dressed, too handsome for his own good, and asks her to predict how he prefers his eggs: <blockquote>
  <i>“What kind of eggs?” I asked.<br>“You tell me.” The boy’s words caught me off guard.<br>I stared at him through the wisps of hair still covering my face. “You want me to guess how you want your eggs cooked?”<br>He smiled. “Why not?”<br>And just like that, the gauntlet was thrown.<br>“Not scrambled,” I said, thinking out loud. Scrambled eggs were too average, too common, and this was a guy who liked to be a little bit different. Not too different, though, which ruled out poached—at least in a place like this. Sunny-side up would have been too messy for him; over hard wouldn’t be messy enough.<br>“Over easy.” I was as sure of the conclusion as I was of the color of his eyes. He smiled and closed his menu.</i>
</blockquote><b>Over easy eggs! Clearly, Cassie is a genius worthy of the FBI.</b> Just like that, she is drafted to join a special unit in the FBI. The Naturals. She lives and trains with four other teenagers, each with their own special skills. They may be kids, but they're soooooooooo much better than the real FBI agents.<br><blockquote>
  <i>No matter how long they did this job, or how much training they had, these agents would never have instincts as finely honed as ours.</i>
</blockquote>Teen <s>Titans</s> Power, YEAH!<br><br>The kids, and they are kids---try to solve old cases for practice, they do training on random everyday subjects at malls, food courts. The teenagers in the prorgam play games, they flirt, they kiss. And there might be a serial killer out there who wants to collect Cassie as his prize.<br><br><b>Let's get this straight, this is Criminal Minds fanfiction, but it does not have an iota of the enjoyability.</b><br><br><u><i>Criminal Minds</i> has amazing, complex characters</u><br>The teens in the Naturals are teenagers. For better or worse. They have special abilities, there is no doubt of that, but <b>I have serious doubts as to their judgment and their competence to actually fulfil their purpose when 90% of the times, they act like---well, really immature teenagers</b>. The characters are teenagers who act positively juvenile; they have special abilities, but that is the limit to my interest towards them. There is nothing about the characters that make them stand out, that make me sympathize with them, that make me like them, despite the author's attempt at giving them sad backstories. They are merely teenagers who get on my nerves.<br><br>We have Dean, who is the James-Dean-esque weightlifting, bulky teenaged deliquent who looks ready to punch someone in the face at any second. Dean is a profiler, like Cassie. We have Lia, the sexy Asian girl, who wants to slither onto Michael's lap at any given second. Her specialty is lying, at detecting liars. We have Michael, the wealthy, (multiple) Porsche-owning trust funded, blue-blooded, smug-as-a-bug-in-a-rug son-of-a-bitch whose sole purpose in life is to make Dean lose control and to make Cassie want to rip his head off (<b>when she's not kissing him, that is</b>). We have Sloane, the duller than dull factoid spouter who is boring, and who's pretty much useless. I mean, anyone can spout off random-ass facts. <b>I would be a much better Sloane. I mean, I have personality.</b><br><br>Cassie herself is boring, without personality. Cassie reminds me of geniuses who are so brilliant in one category that they are completely lacking in everything else in life. Life skills. Personality. Cassie is a good profiler, not great, I have a lot of skepticism where her skills are concerned, and I have to accept the fact that her natural talents are that---natural, inside her, because there is no explaining her talents otherwise. Frankly, Cassie never exhibits many signs of intelligence besides for her Natural Profiling skill.<br><br>The rest of the characters are largely unlikeable in one way or another, they are either surly, or selfish, or bitchy, or snarky, or else they blend into the shadow so much I hardly remember they're there. I think that's why Sloane spouts off so many random facts. If she didn't speak up once in awhile to say something completely random like <i>"Less than point-five percent of the words in the English language contain all five vowels,”</i> I would completely forget that she has ever been there.<br><br><u><i>Criminal Minds</i> does not concern itself about their team playing petty mind games with each other, nor do they play Truth-Or-Dare</u><br>There is so much antipathy between the characters. Dean and Michael are ready to strangle each other at any given second, and while Dean keeps quiet and stay true to his bad-boy-loner trope, Michaels is the Naturals version of <i>The Simpson</i>'s Nelson Muntz, pointing his finger in Dean's face, going HAW-HAW!!!!!!<blockquote>
  <i>“Have you ever seen The Bad Seed?” he inquired politely. “The movie.”<br>A muscle in Dean’s jaw twitched. “No.”<br>Michael grinned. “I have.”<br>Dean stood up. “I’m done here.”</i>
</blockquote>**note: Dean's father is a serial killer, hence the <i>Bad Seed</i> joke. <i>The Bad Seed</i> is a movie where the child turns out to be an evil, murdering monstrosity.**<br><br><u><i>Criminal Minds</i> does not concern itself with a fucking love triangle</u><br>There's Cassie! Who will she fall for?! Is it bad-boy loner Dean? The surly boy who never, ever, EVEEEEEEEEER lets anyone close to his heart---until Cassie comes along! Or will Cassie fall for Michael! Michael with his movie-star good looks and multiple Porsches who hides his nonchalance behind a snarky exterior, never letting anyone see the warm, melty, oozing, cheesy (sorry, I haven't eaten dinner yet), fluffy interior. Over easy, indeed!<br><br>Or will it be Lia! Lia with her constant flirtation with Michael! Or does Lia love Dean instead?! Noooooooooo!<br><br>Fucking gag me, please.<br><br><u><i>Criminal Minds</i> never has a fucking touching romantic moment right after leaving a crime scene with dead bloodied bodies and a killer on the loose</u><br><blockquote>
  <i>When Agent Starmans glanced in the room, all he saw was [him] and me.<br>Kissing.<br>The kiss in the pool was nothing compared to this. Then, our lips had barely brushed. Now, my lips were opening. Our mouths were crushed together. His hand traveled from my neck down to my lower back. My lips tingled, and I leaned into the kiss, shifting my body until I could feel the heat from his in my arms, my chest, my stomach.</i>
</blockquote>Self-explanatory.<br><br><u><i>Criminal Minds</i> has Reid. Sloane is no Reid</u><br>Really, Sloane is the most useless character in the world. She does absolutely nothing besides spouting off random facts:<br><blockquote>
  <i>Sloane on coffee was a bit like an auctioneer on speed. The numbers poured out of her mouth rapid-fire, a statistic for every occasion. For eight hours.<br>“Sixteen percent of American men have blue eyes,” she informed me blithely. “But over forty percent of male TV doctors do.”</i>
</blockquote>Oh, and she's a really good hugger. <b>Because every FBI investigative team needs a hugger. For hugs.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Sloane slipped an arm around my waist. “There are fourteen varieties of hugs,” she said. “This is one of them.”</i>
</blockquote><u><i>Criminal Minds</i> does not try to slut-shame a girl</u><br>Lia. Poor Lia. She is sleek, she is Asian, she is sexy, she is tall. She also has a special ability to lie. She wears barely-there clothes. She makes numerous sexual innuendoes.<br><blockquote>
  <i>Agent Locke added, meeting Lia’s eyes, “she’s a very good liar.”<br>Lia didn’t seem to take offense at the agent’s words. “I’m also bilingual,” she said. “And very, very flexible.”<br>The second very was aimed directly at Michael.</i>
</blockquote>Naturally, she's to be shamed for the way she dresses. Naturally she hits on the guys. Naturally, she eats ice cream for breakfast (in a sexual manner) and wears silk pajamas that leaves nothing to the imagination. <b>Can we not do this, please? Can we just have normal characters who just happen to like dressing that way without writing it in a way so that the reader hates them?</b><br><br>If you want to read books about serial killers, <i>I Hunt Killers</i> by Barry Lyga is a good book. Alternately, you can just go watch <i>Criminal Minds</i> itself. Either way, I can guarantee you will get more enjoyment from either than you will ever get out of this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3821329435830338970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1648969278" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1648969278" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1648969278?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fast-paced">fast-paced</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648969278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11003678975024763064">Who says teenagers can’t be FBI agents?<br/><br/>Definitely not Cassandra Hobbes, a profiler recruited by the FBI to be part of their program.<br/><br/>She analyzes people. She can find the slightest details about someone and use them to solve puzzles. However, the training part of the program isn’t enough for her. She wants to help find real murderers and not play repetitive games that agents believe will prepare her to become the perfect profiler.<br/><br/>Suddenly, an opportunity strikes.<br/><br/>The main problem with this story i</span>
  <span id="freeText11003678975024763064" style="display:none">Who says teenagers can’t be FBI agents?<br /><br />Definitely not Cassandra Hobbes, a profiler recruited by the FBI to be part of their program.<br /><br />She analyzes people. She can find the slightest details about someone and use them to solve puzzles. However, the training part of the program isn’t enough for her. She wants to help find real murderers and not play repetitive games that agents believe will prepare her to become the perfect profiler.<br /><br />Suddenly, an opportunity strikes.<br /><br />The main problem with this story is that it’s too <em>convenient</em>. It’s too convenient that Cassie has a gift, that her mom was murdered and that the biggest case the FBI agents are working on has a direct link to her.<br /><br />It’s just not realistic.<br /><br />And I know you may think that, hey, the teenagers being agents in training thing is not realistic either, so why are you complaining about that… But the thing is <strong>EVERYTHING </strong>revolves around Cassie. Everything.<br /><br />But it’s still fun. It’s fast-paced, intriguing and definitely not predictable. The revelation is very annoying, since I expected more—something more original—but it took me by surprise and that’s what counts.<br /><br />The characters are reminiscent of Cammie, Macey, Liz and Zach from <em>The Gallagher Girls</em> series. I can bet on the fact that Jennifer Lynn Barnes read it before writing this.<br /><br />Cassie is the one who puts pieces together (Cammie), Lia is the human lie detector with attitude (Macey), Sloan is the brains (Liz) and Michael is the quiet, mysterious, possibly dangerous and handsome guy (Zach). Dean, well, he’s a cute one.<br /><br />Even if the plot is far-stretched and annoyingly related to Cassie, I still liked the world-building and the whole idea of a program for <em>Naturals</em>, who are teenagers with different abilities that can come in handy when trying to solve murder cases.<br /><br />The writing is good also. The dynamics between characters will keep anyone entertained and the chapters from the murder’s point of view often gave me goose bumps.<br /><br />Cassie’s narration is interesting, but the problem is she’s <em>aware </em>of the reader. In <em>The Gallagher Girls, </em>Cammie relates everything knowing someone else will read her—let’s call it—journal. But that’s because she has to. In this book, Cassie talks to herself as though she knew that someone is reading her thoughts, and that makes the story even more inauthentic.<br /><br />But again, it’s not bad. I liked it. If I could, I would change many things about it, but I needed something different and I got it. Relatively.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11003678975024763064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText8695504331847831707" style="display:none">1.) The Naturals ★★★★.5<br />2.) Killer Instinct ★★★★<br />3.) All In ★★★★.5<br />4.) Bad Blood ★★★★.5<br /><br />--------------------------------------------------<br /><br />REREAD OCTOBER 2017<br />Wasn't as good as the first time because obviously I knew who the killer was, but still, this series is so good!<br /><br />JANUARY 2016<br />*4.5 STARS* <br />WOW. What a way to start off my reading year! This literally is a YA version of Criminal Minds with a tiny paranormal twist. The FBI has found and recruited some teenagers who are 'naturals' at certain abilities that the FBI want to trial in a new program that could help to solve some cold cases. The main character Cassie is a natural profiler and ever since she stumbled across the scene of her mother's murder (although her body was never found), she's felt like something in her life was missing. She meets these new people and learns all about profiling and victimology and it's just SO exciting I literally read this book in ONE sitting! There is a love triangle introduced which at first had me real angry, but thankfully the characters realised they had more important things to worry about so that was really put on the back burner while they were trying to find a particular serial killer that WAS SO CRAZY. I literally did not see anything coming, which let's be honest, is kinda rare these days in a YA book. I absolutely LOVED this and I can't wait to continue on with the series!<br /><br />Around the Year in 52 Books Challenge Notes:<br />- 31. A YA book</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1042209722695455798">You know what <b>astounds</b> me about these MCs in YA literature??<br/><br/><b>Their level of self-confidence</b> which easily, and almost always, <b>borders on the self-centered/self-delusional-ness territory.</b><br/><br/>I truly can't imagine anyone would hurt other people for my sake at all, let alone to actually end their lives. <br/><br/>But nope, not a problem for our Cassie here.   <span id="freeText1042209722695455798" style="display:none">You know what <b>astounds</b> me about these MCs in YA literature??<br /><br /><b>Their level of self-confidence</b> which easily, and almost always, <b>borders on the self-centered/self-delusional-ness territory.</b><br /><br />I truly can't imagine anyone would hurt other people for my sake at all, let alone to actually end their lives. <br /><br />But nope, not a problem for our Cassie here. Cassie who almost casually stated <i>"I knew suddenly that he could pull the trigger. He wouldn’t hesitate. If he thought I was in danger, he would put a bullet in the other guy’s head.”</i><br /><br />And all this after they had known each other for what? A decade? Ha! If only. No, she met him a month / few months ago. There was no solid timeline from what I remember. But i’m sure those were the most ‘epic’ weeks of their lives *eyeroll*<br /><br />A lot of times, the book feels overreaching with all the incredibly <i>unnatural</i> 'naturals' abilities. While the writing and mystery/story were decent enough, the book would have benefited so much from not having this perplexing, pointless love triangle in it - just felt like adding another layer of unbelievableness to an already unrealistic book to me.<br /><br /><br /><b>rating: ★★</b><br /><br /><br />====================<br /><br /><br />The cover is so simple and so effing creepy!! <br /><br />Is that a promise??<br /><br />I'll hold you to it, Book.<br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_697892996" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/697892996?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=2013">2013</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=boring-narrative">boring-narrative</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=drama">drama</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=1st-in-series">1st-in-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer697892996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15457142108790638909"><a href='http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238998i/681660._SX540_.png' height='120' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>Man, this was such a huge letdown.<br/><br/>I was really looking forward to this book because I thought I'd finally get to read something like Criminal Minds or Lie To Me or, heck, even CSI. I loved those shows; I gobbled them all up when I first learned about their existence. The Naturals promised me that, but unfortunately, it was a disappointment all around.<br/><br/><b>These are what The Naturals consists of:</b><br/><br/>* 50% drama from an unnecessary love triangle;<br/>* 20% of Cassie overthinking things, apart from being dul</span>
  <span id="freeText15457142108790638909" style="display:none"><a href="http://thesocialpotato.maryfaye.net" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238998i/681660._SX540_.png" height="120" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>Man, this was such a huge letdown.<br><br>I was really looking forward to this book because I thought I'd finally get to read something like Criminal Minds or Lie To Me or, heck, even CSI. I loved those shows; I gobbled them all up when I first learned about their existence. The Naturals promised me that, but unfortunately, it was a disappointment all around.<br><br><b>These are what The Naturals consists of:</b><br><br>* 50% drama from an unnecessary love triangle;<br>* 20% of Cassie overthinking things, apart from being dull and lifeless;<br>* 20% of the characters being self-centered narcissists, basking in all their supposed talents and glories; and<br>* 10% actual plot<br><br>Of course, I should have expected this given that it's, after all, Young Adult, but it's kind of hard not to feel bummed out when you expected a story that actually explores the psyche of a criminal without being pretentious about it. It was already hard enough to suspend my disbelief of the super prestigious FBI hiring a bunch of teenagers who are supposedly "natural" at reading emotions, spotting liars, reading someone's psyche, and are actually better than their adult counterparts who do this for a living, but for this book to add insult to injury... ugh. <br><br>Let me better explain my frustrations:<br><br>1.) <b>Cassie.</b> Throughout reading the book, I did not feel for this girl at all. I did not root for her, I did not like her. PERIOD. She was amazingly bland, and her 1st person narration felt like reading someone narrate a story from a detached point of view. Every time something huge happened, she sounded absolutely monotonous in describing "her feelings" (and there were honestly very little...) and the surroundings that the events turned out more anti-climactic than anything else.<br><br>She's also nosy. Dear woman, if the guy doesn't want to spill his secrets yet, don't freaking force him. God, you make me crazy.<br><br>And she over-thinks. A LOT. I mean, okay, I guess if you're a Natural profiler (yes, with a capital N, as portrayed in the book), that's a given, but god, could she be please less pretentious and all-high-and-mighty about it? I get that she's perceptive, but sweet baby Jesus, it annoyed me to no end how she would see someone do something in a particular manner and immediately conclude, "Ah, this person is like this! Ah, that person is like that!"<br><br>And yes, I get it, Cassie. You're a Natural. You're so good at observing people. You are SO perceptive. I get it. Stop rubbing it in.<br><br>2.) <b>Side characters.</b> The other characters have personalities, but they're so cheesy and unoriginal. We have a cocky guy who thinks he's all that and who's smug all the time who can read emotions, we have the loner guy who has a dark tragic past who's also a profiler, we have a bitchy girl who can spot lies, and we have a quirky girl who's supposedly like Reid from Criminal Minds, who can give you statistics for the most mundane of things. Can they not be anymore stereotypical? T_T<br><br>AND YES, I GET IT. YOU'RE ALL FUCKING NATURALS!!! Is there a need to repeat your extraordinary talents over and over???<br><br>3.) <b>Unnecessary love triangle.</b> UGH. This part made me roll my eyes SO MUCH. As expected, the bland heroine enters the fray and the two guys in the team, of course, suddenly take an interest in her. She hasn't done anything redeeming, she has no fucking personality, and I'm supposed to believe they both like her already? What the flying fuck?<br><br>One of the cheesiest moments in this novel was how they all decided to play a game of Truth or Dare (LOL!!!!!!) and of course she was dared to kiss one of them... OF COURSE... That had my eyes rolling around and around and around like a ferris wheel. And of course, the other guy strikes back by kissing her again later... and OF COURSE the heroine is torn between her feelings for the two as she's always blushing at both of them T_T AHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH. And of course, by the end of the book, we still have no idea who she's inclined to like more.<br><br>What saved it from becoming a 1 star was the ending and the plot that was present in the last 15 or so percent. A bit predictable, but it was interesting. There's also no cliffhanger, and it ends nicely in a way there's still room for more content in the future books. <br><br>Just fix this nonsense love triangle and add a personality in the heroine please and this could be better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15457142108790638909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_531769413" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/531769413" />
    <a title="Veronica Morfi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5510829-veronica-morfi"><img alt="Veronica Morfi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419153500p2/5510829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/531769413?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica Morfi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica Morfi" href="/user/show/5510829-veronica-morfi">Veronica Morfi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer531769413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15941161916630663197">Rating: 4.5/5<br/><br/>The Naturals is a great book for fans of Criminal Minds, CSI and shows like them. I am a fan of all those kind of shows and when I read the blurb of this book I was dying to get my hands on it. And I am really glad I did. This had mystery, murder, serieal killers, kids with powers (not exactly supernatural powers bu still...), romance, fighting. It was just perfect. Exactly what I was looking for.<br/><br/>The Naturals are a group of teenagers that are trained by the FBI to solve mostly cold </span>
  <span id="freeText15941161916630663197" style="display:none">Rating: 4.5/5<br><br>The Naturals is a great book for fans of Criminal Minds, CSI and shows like them. I am a fan of all those kind of shows and when I read the blurb of this book I was dying to get my hands on it. And I am really glad I did. This had mystery, murder, serieal killers, kids with powers (not exactly supernatural powers bu still...), romance, fighting. It was just perfect. Exactly what I was looking for.<br><br>The Naturals are a group of teenagers that are trained by the FBI to solve mostly cold cases of serieal killers. All five kids have some amazing powers. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418890127ra/12938835.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418890127ra/12938836.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418890127ra/12938837.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418890127ra/12938838.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418890127ra/12938839.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After Cassie joins the group some strange murders start happening close to town. Women are found dead, their faces curved up. Half of them are red-heads and half of them worked as psychics. Cassie's mom was both and she was also murdered 5 years ago with no clue of where her body was. Cassie believes that this case is connected to her mother's and she is determined to find the killer.<br><br>If the description so far haven't caught your eye let me tell you that this book was absolutely amazing. There were five teenagers living in the same house, with all the drama that may cause. We got to get inside the killers mind with a few chapters from a YOU point of view, those were the creepiest ones. Also it was amazing to see the little details that profilers use to find out more about the UNSUBs and their victims. <br><br>I also really enjoyed the romance in this one. Even though it is a love triangle it's so perfectly done that I still don't know who Cassie will choose. Usually it's so easy to tell, it's like the third person is there just for argument's sake. But in this one both Michael and Dean have this great chemistry with Cassie. They are very different and mysterious and I have no idea what's going to happen with them.<br><br>All in all, this was fast-paced, action paked, full of serial killers, mystery, following clues and unique characters. I can't wait for the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15941161916630663197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2160359416" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2160359416" />
    <a title="bella farren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23223005-bella-farren"><img alt="bella farren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598064440p2/23223005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2160359416?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="bella farren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="bella farren" href="/user/show/23223005-bella-farren">bella farren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781780876825" href="/book/show/18591093-the-naturals">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23223005-bella-farren?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23223005-bella-farren?shelf=love-triangles">love-triangles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23223005-bella-farren?shelf=mystery-thrillers-suspense">mystery-thrillers-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23223005-bella-farren?shelf=angsty">angsty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2160359416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2230520943976611530"><b>2.5/5</b><br/><br/><blockquote> <i>“Sloane slipped an arm around my waist. "There are fourteen varieties of hugs," she said. "This is one of them.” </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>This book sparked my interest when I saw it <b>marketed as a teenage Criminal Minds</b>, teens with natural talents (such as profiling, statistics, detection of deception and emotion), being recruited by the FBI to help crack cold cases. <br/><br/>The few things that peaked my interest didn't really come to fruition, there wasn't much to compare to Criminal Minds and there was no cracking of co</span>
  <span id="freeText2230520943976611530" style="display:none"><b>2.5/5</b><br><br><blockquote> <i>“Sloane slipped an arm around my waist. "There are fourteen varieties of hugs," she said. "This is one of them.” </i>
</blockquote><br><br>This book sparked my interest when I saw it <b>marketed as a teenage Criminal Minds</b>, teens with natural talents (such as profiling, statistics, detection of deception and emotion), being recruited by the FBI to help crack cold cases. <br><br>The few things that peaked my interest didn't really come to fruition, there wasn't much to compare to Criminal Minds and there was no cracking of cold cases. The 'serial killer' case that this story followed wasn't a main point until the last quarter, which meant the majority of the book dragged. <br><br>This book was more of a bad teenage drama than a YA thriller, and I didn't enjoy the petty going's on. The dramas began pretty early on when the main character, seventeen year old Cassie, is removed from the care of her family and into the FBI safe house where four other teenaged FBI 'naturals' lived. There was a painful teenage love triangle (no real surprise there) and the usual girl/girl bitchiness. <br><br>The only teenage character I actually enjoyed was Sloane, who was a beautiful and pure soul. She was adorably terrible at anything social and was easily bribed with coffee. So, a lot like me.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511080922ra/24481041.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I get what the author was trying to achieve by using teenagers, but I felt like it wasn't executed in the best way. There was no real mention of any of the teens' family, and even the main character's family wasn't mentioned after she left their care. The whole story seemed pretty unbelievable, mostly because they were all minors. <br><br>My biggest issue was without a doubt, the teenage angst. I have a younger sister who is the definition of teenage angst (seriously, look up the definition and she's listed as a an example) and as much as I love her, she's used up my limit for teenage angst. It made my skin crawl, I was here for serial killers and kickass teenage crime solvers, and I got a <b>fucking love triangle.</b> The only thing worse than a love triangle, is a <i>teenage</i> love triangle. I think you get my message at this point, teenage <s>anything</s> angst is not my favourite thing. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463484944ra/19122857.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Unfortunately, I guessed the plot and killer pretty early on, picking up the <s>supposedly</s> subtle clues. Still, I enjoyed the actual crime fighting section of the book and the little chapters in the killer's point of view were a nice touch. There were a few loose ends and plot holes that disappointed me a little, but the overall serial killer plot line was intriguing. <br><br>Lastly, <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511080923ra/24481042.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>authors, pls stop w/ these love triangles. they suck. u suck.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2230520943976611530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1556293269" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1556293269" />
    <a title="Maggie ☘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie"><img alt="Maggie ☘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591529603p2/40477684.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1556293269?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maggie ☘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maggie ☘" href="/user/show/40477684-maggie">Maggie ☘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=great-reads-2016">great-reads-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=charismatic-characters">charismatic-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=interesting-villains-antiheroes">interesting-villains-antiheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=contemporary-na">contemporary-na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=ya-mystery-crime-fiction">ya-mystery-crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=amazing-reads">amazing-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=tbr-or-to-buy">tbr-or-to-buy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=superpowers">superpowers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40477684-maggie?shelf=underrated-gems">underrated-gems</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1556293269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9412139640741144783"><b>
  <i>“None of us had normal childhoods," Sloane said quietly. "If we had, we wouldn't be Naturals.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>This is kind of unusual review for me, since I've already read the first three book in this series (In very record time!) Actually finished the third book - <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24849026.All_In__The_Naturals___3_' title='All In (The Naturals, #3) by Jennifer Lynn Barnes' rel='nofollow noopener'>All In</a> - just right now. This review will be completely spoiler free for all three books, I just want to mention a few of my thoughts on the characters and <i>The Naturals</i> series overall. I have to say that the first book was just a starter, <b>each b</b></span>
  <span id="freeText9412139640741144783" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“None of us had normal childhoods," Sloane said quietly. "If we had, we wouldn't be Naturals.”</i>
</b><br><br>This is kind of unusual review for me, since I've already read the first three book in this series (In very record time!) Actually finished the third book - <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24849026.All_In__The_Naturals___3_" title="All In (The Naturals, #3) by Jennifer Lynn Barnes" rel="nofollow noopener">All In</a> - just right now. This review will be completely spoiler free for all three books, I just want to mention a few of my thoughts on the characters and <i>The Naturals</i> series overall. I have to say that the first book was just a starter, <b>each book is better than the former, and it all comes amazingly together in the third one</b>! (Which is also my favourite so far and I don't think any other book from this series can surpass that one). So definitely recommended. Go read this series, people!<br><br>This is my second series from Jennifer Lynn Barnes (the first one being <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22929578.The_Fixer__The_Fixer__1_" title="The Fixer (The Fixer #1) by Jennifer Lynn Barnes" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fixer</a>), which I both adored, and now I can safely say I'm going to read her other novels as well, especially her crimi/ psychological series. Because even though I haven't read any fantasy by her yet, I think she'd be best at these kinds of books. <br><br><br><b>
  <i>“Every person in this house was fundamentally screwed up to the depths of our dark and shadowy souls.”</i>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479161345i/21155211._SY540_.png" width="330" height="410" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><i>The Naturals</i> series is <b>highly addictive, intriguing and gripping Young Adult crime series</b> which mainly centers on five people, each with special abilities to solve crimes and catch serial killers for FBI.<br><br>It was seriously such a page-turner for me! Obviously, since I didn't give it full five stars, it's not perfect. There's some teen drama and indecisiveness regarding the romance going on here in the first two books, but do not fear, the third book had no such thing! (And here I was fearing while reading book one that the love triangle would stretch till the last book. Surprise, surprise!) But even then there were much more important things going on in this series than the romance, it never took center stage in my opinion. <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479161919i/21155237._SY540_.png" width="340" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><i>
  <b>“Agent Sterling turned back to the boxes on her bed. “When the odds are bad,” she said, removing something from one of them, “you change the rules.”</b>
</i><br><br><br>The plot flows swiftly and there aren't many dull moments, <b>the mysteries in every book are pretty dark and inteligently written</b>. There were always some little hints here and there throughout the stories, and each investigation was greatly done. I guessed some of the identities of the killers alongside the characters, but <b> some other plot-twists were hugely surprising</b>! So if you get through the fact that it's about <b>five teenagers who are working for the FBI and solving murders</b> (and even though there are some restrictions, the authorities ultimately lets them), <b>this series is very clever</b>. (Just like The Fixer, which is btw also recommended!)<br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479161768i/21155231._SY540_.png" width="320" height="430" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <i>“Nothing hurts you unless you let it.”</i>
</b><br><br><br>It's clear to see that Jennifer Lynn Barnes studied psychology and has degree in cognitive science (the study of the brain and thought), because <b>none of these characters</b> (even the side ones) <b>are flat, and as the series progresses they only become more layered and complicated. Believable.</b> <br>Every last one of them gets the attention he/she deserves - the main heroine, the other four kids, the old marine sniper who's taking care of them, the FBI agents and of course, the killers. I was especially very surprised about the YOU chapters. <br><b>The story is not only told from the point of view of our main heroine Cassie, but also from each different killer in every book.</b> These little chapters were suprisingly and sometimes sickeningly detailed, which was pretty surprising for YA in my opinion. The author doesn't play nice with her readers, <b>she makes them loathe the villains, but also understand their motives, the histories that made them into the monsters they are. It's fascinating.</b> <br><br><i>
  <b>“Some people said that broken bones grew back stronger. On the good days, I told myself that was true, that each time the world tried to break me, I became a little less breakable. On the bad days, I suspected that I would always be broken, that parts of me would never be quite right—and that those were the parts that made me good at the job.<br>Those were the parts that made this house and the people in it home.”</b>
</i><br><br><br>✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨✨✨✨<br><br><b>➵ Cassie Hobbes - <br>Natural Ability: <u>The Profiler</u></b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479162278i/21155270.png" width="410" height="295" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>She's ultimately great and very <b>relatable main heroine</b>. Sometimes she acts too much teenagey, especially in the beginning of this series, but <b>can surprise you with her mind and courage</b>. <br>As the series goes, her characters gets through more and more trials, have some battle scars, but lives, survives and becomes so much more fascinating than she was before.<br><br><br>✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨✨✨✨<br><br><br><b>➵ Dean Redding - <br>Natural Ability: <u>The Profiler</u></b><br><br><b>
  <i>“Maybe, to do what you and I do, we have to have a little bit of monsters in us.”</i>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479162557i/21155303._SX540_.png" width="450" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's pretty hard to decide since all five of the characters are distinctive and amazing but <b>I think he comes as my favourite from them</b>. <br>I can't say too much about him, because hello spoilers, but his history, his struggles... I can definitely understand why he wouldn't want people close after that, why he'd have problems to open up, his low sense of worth, his fear of himself. <br>All of it was so well done, so <b>psychologically intriguing, dark and painful</b>. One cannot help but be fascinated and maybe a little in love with his character. <br><br><br>✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨✨✨✨<br><br><br><b>➵ Lia Zhang -<br>Natural Ability: <u>Deception Specialist</u></b> <br><br><b>
  <i>“Too young to party, just old enough to participate in federal investigations of serial murder.” Lia let out an elaborate sigh. “Story of my life.”</i>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479162404i/21155284.png" width="410" height="290" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>When she first stormed on the scene, I thought for sure there will be once again the annoying ex-girlfriend who hates the MC for no reason whatsoever and girl hate over a guy.. Well, surprise surprise! This is not the case. Yes, sometimes it seems that she hates Cassie, but there's more to it than that. She has problems with trust, she doesn't show people her real self, because she's protecting herself from them in a way. <b>There's definitely no insta-friendship between Cassie and Lia, I love their interactions anyway.</b> Her past is very complicated <b>- Ok, you can just note here that EVERYONE'S past is complicated here. And I mean it in the best possible way -</b> and truth be said I still don't know all of it, <b>she's complex and layered character</b> like that! It takes some time to truly know who she is, to know when she tells the truth and when she deceives. <b>She hides under layers of different personalities</b>, she can lie and detect lies effortlessly. Alongside with Dean, she's the most fascinating character, and I love her probably just as much as him.<br><br><br>✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨✨✨✨<br><br><br><b>➵ Michael Townsend -<br>Natural Ability: <u>Emotion Reader</u></b><br><br><b>
  <i>“Luckily for us, I've never met a bad idea I did not immediately embrace like the dearest of friends.” </i>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479162466i/21155294.png" width="410" height="290" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I don't have that much to say about him, besides the fact that he is <b>pretty fun character</b> (but in no way as amazing and fun as Asher from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22929578.The_Fixer__The_Fixer__1_" title="The Fixer (The Fixer #1) by Jennifer Lynn Barnes" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fixer</a>!)<br>I admit, I have kind of hate to like relationship with this guy. His past wasn't all sunshine and roses either, but <b>I just didn't really love to him like I did the others. Mainly because this guy seemed like such a player, that's why I preferred Dean with Cassie and Michael with Lia from the get go of this book. Lia could handle him more, and personality wise, they seem like a much better fit.</b> Plus he has some serious anger issues, which I would normally loathe to read about, but in his case I think it was understandable, well done psychologically and he was in no way abusive toward Cassie or Lia, so there's that. <b>Overall I did like him. Only, he's my least favourite from the five.</b><br>And yes, there's a love-triangle again.. Sigh.. Which is one of the few things about this series that I didn't really like. It was unecessary. And now after finishing book three, I breathe a sigh of relief, because there was none now.<br><br><br>✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨✨✨✨<br><br><br><b>➵ Sloane Tarvish - <br>Natural ability: <u>Numerical Expert</u></b><br><br><b>
  <i>“I wondered how much of Sloane’s fascination with numbers had arisen during moments like this one, when numbers were easy and people were hard.”</i>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479162809i/21155323._SX540_.png" width="450" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>She's just such a sweet character! <b>Sloane love numbers and statistics.</b> She's practically a walking Encyclopedia and Wikipedia in one.<br>Sloane doesn't really understand basic 'normal' human interactions and relationships. <b>She experiences and deals with emotions in slightly different way</b>, when she can't deal with them, she obsessively does something else, mostly her work for the cases. She's <b>highly intelligent</b>. Loves math and statistics. I adore this girl, but really... can't relate.<br><br><br>✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨ ✨✨✨✨<br><br><br><b>
  <i>“It's not the bad memories that tear a person apart. It's the good ones.” </i>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446580878i/16835263._SY540_.png" width="320" height="430" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><b>All in all, intelligent Ya Crimi series about five teens with special abilities</b> (not paranormal) who solve murders, try to save people, form different relationships and <b>even in their new lives, past comes haunting them each back eventually</b>. <b>The psychological matters are greatly and believably done</b>, the investigations intriguing and plot addictive. I would without doubt recommend for you to give <i>The Naturals</i> a try. <br><br><b><i>“Home isn't a place, Cassie.' The memory crept up on me. 'Home is the people who love you most, the people who will always love you, forever and ever, no matter what.”</i> </b><br><br><br>------------------------------------<br><br>My rating of <i>The Naturals</i> series - <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13597723.The_Naturals__The_Naturals___1_" title="The Naturals (The Naturals, #1) by Jennifer Lynn Barnes" rel="nofollow noopener">The Naturals</a> ★★★★☆ (4/5 stars)<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20409231.Killer_Instinct__The_Naturals___2_" title="Killer Instinct (The Naturals, #2) by Jennifer Lynn Barnes" rel="nofollow noopener">Killer Instinct</a> ★★★★☆ (4.5/5 stars)<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24849026.All_In__The_Naturals___3_" title="All In (The Naturals, #3) by Jennifer Lynn Barnes" rel="nofollow noopener">All In</a> ★★★★★ (5/5 stars)<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27424547.Bad_Blood__The_Naturals___4_" title="Bad Blood (The Naturals, #4) by Jennifer Lynn Barnes" rel="nofollow noopener">Bad Blood</a> ★★★★★ (5/5 stars)<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36160420.Twelve__The_Naturals___4_5_" title="Twelve (The Naturals, #4.5) by Jennifer Lynn Barnes" rel="nofollow noopener">Twelve</a> ★★★★★ (5/5 stars)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9412139640741144783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2096551222" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2096551222" />
    <a title="Nadia Awadi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35852954-nadia-awadi"><img alt="Nadia Awadi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518955546p2/35852954.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2096551222?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadia Awadi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadia Awadi" href="/user/show/35852954-nadia-awadi">Nadia Awadi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2096551222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6828739626263038604"><b>Love triangles are the bane of enjoying YA books peacefully.</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458878581ra/18542752.gif' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>First of all, let me tell you about how I read this series and DNF'ed it.<br/><br/><i>Innocent 16-year-old Nedia stumbled upon a series called THE NATURALS. She liked the series. The series liked her back. She found a fictional boyfriend called Michael. She started shipping Michael and Cassie. Nedia was certain that they will end up together. How could they not? But, Oh, no! Nedia was so so wrong. She shipped the wrong ship. That ship was sinking. A</i></span>
  <span id="freeText6828739626263038604" style="display:none"><b>Love triangles are the bane of enjoying YA books peacefully.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458878581ra/18542752.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>First of all, let me tell you about how I read this series and DNF'ed it.<br><br><i>Innocent 16-year-old Nedia stumbled upon a series called THE NATURALS. She liked the series. The series liked her back. She found a fictional boyfriend called Michael. She started shipping Michael and Cassie. Nedia was certain that they will end up together. How could they not? But, Oh, no! Nedia was so so wrong. She shipped the wrong ship. That ship was sinking. And that's how Nedia left the ship and the series. And looked into the sunset with tears running down her face. Then she read a lot of other books, ate chocolate and shipped other people.</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1510672042ra/24439665.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Beautiful story, I know. I came back to finish the series while keeping in mind to ship Cassie and Dean. And now, I can see how Dean is the bad boy with a dark past who needs a hug. I DO. Yet, the author had so many good scenes with Michael and Cassie. SO MANY. I was deceived!<br><br>I will just stop being dramatic and talk about the book.<br><br><u>Rating</u> <i>
  <b>4,5- should've been 5 but the love triangle ruined it-stars.</b>
</i><br><br><u>
  <b>The Plot</b>
</u><br><br><i>Cassie has been always good at reading people. Figuring them out. A skill that gets her into a special program for the FBI where she will use her ability to catch serial killers. Her first case is related to her mother's death. Will Cassie be able to solve the case? or is the killer too clever?</i><br><br>The plot was interesting, fast paced and will keep you at the edge of your seat. It's also original. Its greatest aspect is the killer's chapters. It's so creepy and weirdly entertaining.<br><br><br><u>
  <b>The Characters</b>
</u><br><br><b>Cassie</b><br>Despite being in a love triangle. She was a decent character. She's a natural profiler. I really liked the fact that she was level-headed through it all: Her mother's murder, FBI and serial killers. She always got her emotions under control and analysed everything. BUT when it came to love. She was like: <i>What's happening to me? Michael is so beautiful, witty and mysterious. Dean is such a bad boy, with lean muscle and a dark past. Michael or Dean? Dean or Michael?</i> To be honest, I don't mind love triangles that much when the real ship is obvious. But this book played with my emotions.<br><br><b>Michael</b><br>He's so mysterious. Has a mask under his mask. Sometimes an ass-hole. But most of the time, a lonely soul who cares for Cassie. He made me laugh. And I just really liked him. He was so dreamy.<br>He's also a natural who has a knack for reading people's emotions.<br><br><b>Dean</b><br>Now, that I'm twenty. I know that Dean is THE ONE. In all honesty, I should've loved him. He's kind of a lost puppy with a dark past. BUT he was too withdrawn even for my taste. And we don't see that much of him in this book. He's also a natural profiler. Just like Cassie. *I'm rolling my eyes*<br><br><b>Lia</b><br>She's a pathological liar and detects any lie. Super interesting. And likes trouble.<br><br><b>Sloan</b><br>Another great character, with a skill related to statistics and probabilities. Knows a lot of random scary facts. And weirdly sweet.<br><br><u>
  <b>The writing</b>
</u><br>pretty good but doesn't stand out.<br><br><u>
  <b>Why I recommend this book</b>
</u><br>*Original plot<br>*fast paced<br>*Action packed<br>*Psychopath's chapters<br>*Pretty short<br>*Great cast of characters<br><br>Even though, I had a problem with the love triangle, I still really enjoyed this book. I think this series is underrated and I hope more people give it a chance. I'm just salty I didn't get the ship right the first time.<br><br><i>
  <b>Thank you for reading this review, and I hope you enjoyed it.</b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6828739626263038604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_754426550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/754426550" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/754426550?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781780876825" href="/book/show/18591093-the-naturals">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=thriller-crime">thriller-crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer754426550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5260231920288955473"><b>Muuuuuurder.</b> That's all that needs be said, peoples. Go read this book because there's serial killers and murders and bone-chilling plot twists. I love reading these kind of books, but am I ever frightened? Um, nope. I always feel like it's definitely a book and not reality. BUT THIS WAS COMPLETELY DIFFERENT! I was soooo sucked in, I actually felt my stomach churning. It's <i>so incredibly well written</i> it just blows my mind.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426243906ra/13991901.gif' width='245' height='185' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>The only reason it's not getting 5-stars is I felt a bit detached.</b> A few ti</span>
  <span id="freeText5260231920288955473" style="display:none"><b>Muuuuuurder.</b> That's all that needs be said, peoples. Go read this book because there's serial killers and murders and bone-chilling plot twists. I love reading these kind of books, but am I ever frightened? Um, nope. I always feel like it's definitely a book and not reality. BUT THIS WAS COMPLETELY DIFFERENT! I was soooo sucked in, I actually felt my stomach churning. It's <i>so incredibly well written</i> it just blows my mind.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426243906ra/13991901.gif" width="245" height="185" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The only reason it's not getting 5-stars is I felt a bit detached.</b> A few times I was just speed reading because I felt there was a lot of "filler" material (I had to catch myself a reread a few pages). And the romance? Ergh. The romance felt completely unnecessary. I like how Cassie confesses she's not sure she'll ever be able to love someone (serious tragic childhood trauma sufferer here, peoples) but that doesn't stop her from kissing two different guys in like, um, 2 days. I kind of felt she was leading them on equally at the same time = she didn't care. She's not ready to have a romance! I get that she's a bundle of confusion and stress. I GET THIS. But I'm never fond of love-triangles and this one wasn't any better.<br><br>I also I question the reality of gathering 5 or so gifted kids and then getting them to solve cold cases. It's cooool, but shouldn't they go to school and stuff, also?! They're literally sitting about the house, no wonder they're all psychotic. <br><br><b>The characters are all so REAL.</b> Usually secondary characters are like...you know, never as good as the MC. But in this case?! They had SO much personality. I loved Lia and Sloane. They were slightly crazy and compulsive. I wanted to slap Lia several times but THAT'S WHY SHE'S AMAZING. She's like the annoying little sister. Then there's Dean (the dark broody one) and Michael (the guarded but quirky one) and while I liked them both, I felt their rivalry over Cassie was eye-roll worthy. Cassie...she was cool. I think she had a complex personality, but I just wasn't as interested in her. She seemed so soft and timid for this kind of book/lifestyle. And I don't think she was <i>supposed</i> to be timid. ANYWAY. I'M RAMBLING. Moving on, shall we?!<br><br><b>The writing is fabulous.</b> It's tight, it's not wordy, they cut out the crap and just get to the GOOD STUFF. Even the middle (which I accused of feeling like "filler") isn't boring, so much, as padding out the story. You know? I was really quite desperate to know the answer to the murders. <br><br><b>And, let's not forget...IT'S FREAKY.</b> It's the most realistic serial killer book I've read and everyone's reactions were A+ and I kind of, um, freaked a few times. Which <i>never</i> happens. (And I watch a heck of a lot of crime shows.) Also, can we just take a moment to say criminal profiling is awesome?! HOW COOL IS THAT. It's like Sherlock. And I also saw a lot of the TV show Psych in here, with Cassie profiling people off details around them. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426312096ra/14001366.gif" width="500" height="282" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I REALLY LIKED THIS BOOK.</b> I definitely want the sequels. Like. Um. NOW. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="5260231920288955473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
